## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and concentration in a chemical reaction. This is a classic chemical kinetics problem where the rate law relates the reaction rate to the concentration of reactants, possibly with time-dependent effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Zero-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0', 'scenario': 'Constant rate independent of concentration, e.g., enzyme-saturated reactions'}
- {'name': 'First-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to concentration (radioactive decay, simple decomposition)'}
- {'name': 'Second-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to square of concentration (bimolecular reactions)'}
- {'name': 'General n-th order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1', 'scenario': 'Power-law rate dependence on concentration with fractional or integer order'}
- {'name': 'Mixed-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Combination of first and second order processes (parallel reactions)'}
- {'name': 'Reversible first-order reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1', 'scenario': 'First-order forward and reverse reactions approaching equilibrium'}
- {'name': 'Autocatalytic reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)', 'scenario': 'Product catalyzes its own formation, logistic-type kinetics'}
- {'name': 'Substrate inhibition kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2)', 'scenario': 'Enzyme kinetics with substrate inhibition at high concentrations'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent first-order decay', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'Rate constant changes exponentially with time (catalyst deactivation)'}
- {'name': 'Consecutive reaction rate', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t)', 'scenario': 'Sum of exponential terms from consecutive or parallel reaction pathways'}
- {'name': 'Power-law with offset', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2', 'scenario': 'n-th order kinetics with a constant source or sink term'}
- {'name': 'Monod-type kinetics (decay form)', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1)', 'scenario': 'Saturation kinetics where rate plateaus at high concentration'}
- {'name': 'Sigmoidal cooperative kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (A**c1 + c2)', 'scenario': 'Cooperative binding or allosteric enzyme kinetics'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative dA/dt with positive A suggests consumption/decay kinetics â†’ rate = -k * A^n with k > 0
- Rate approaching zero as Aâ†’0 suggests concentration-dependent kinetics â†’ power-law or rational forms in A
- Rate that levels off at high A suggests saturation â†’ rational fraction A/(A+c) structure
- Rate that passes through a maximum then decreases suggests autocatalysis or substrate inhibition â†’ A*(c-A) or A/(1+A^2)
- If dA/dt depends only on A and not explicitly on t, the system is autonomous â†’ pure f(A) rate law
- Curvature in log(dA/dt) vs log(A) plot deviating from linearity suggests mixed-order or saturation kinetics
- Rate proportional to product of concentration and remaining capacity â†’ A*(K-A) logistic-type term
- Multiple timescales in the data suggest superposition of exponential terms â†’ sum of c*exp(k*t) terms
